<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Poverty</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Poor" redirects here. <p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

near <a href="/wiki/Dadaab" title="Dadaab">Dadaab</a>, Kenya</div></div></div></div>
<p><b>Poverty</b> is the state of having few material possessions or little <a href="/wiki/Income" title="Income">income</a>. Poverty can have diverse <a href="/wiki/Social" title="Social">social</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economic" title="Economic">economic</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political" title="Political">political</a> causes and effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> When evaluating poverty in statistics or economics there are two main measures: <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Absolute_poverty" title="Absolute poverty">absolute poverty</a></i> compares income against the amount needed to meet <a href="/wiki/Basic_needs" title="Basic needs">basic personal needs</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Food" title="Food">food</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clothing" title="Clothing">clothing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shelter_(building)" title="Shelter (building)">shelter</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unesco.org_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-unesco.org-2">[2]</a></sup> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relative_poverty" title="Relative poverty">relative poverty</a></i> measures when a person cannot meet a minimum level of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Living_standards" title="Living standards">living standards</a>, compared to others in the same time and place. The definition of <i>relative poverty</i> varies from one country to another, or from one <a href="/wiki/Society" title="Society">society</a> to another.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unesco.org_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-unesco.org-2">[2]</a></sup>
</p><p>Statistically, as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, most of the world's population live in poverty: in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Purchasing_Power_Parity" title="Purchasing Power Parity">PPP</a> dollars, 85% of people live on less than $30 per day, two-thirds live on less than $10 per day, and 10% live on less than $1.90 per day (extreme poverty).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OWiD_EP_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-OWiD_EP-3">[3]</a></sup> According to the World Bank Group in 2020, more than 40% of the poor live in conflict-affected countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Even when countries experience <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">economic development</a>, the poorest citizens of middle-income countries frequently do not gain an adequate share of their countries' increased wealth to leave poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Governments and non-governmental organizations have experimented with a number of different policies and programs for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poverty_alleviation" title="Poverty alleviation">poverty alleviation</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Rural_electrification" title="Rural electrification">electrification in rural areas</a> or <a href="/wiki/Housing_First" title="Housing First">housing first policies</a> in urban areas. The international policy frameworks for poverty alleviation, established by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in 2015, are summarized in <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_1" title="Sustainable Development Goal 1">Sustainable Development Goal 1: "No Poverty"</a>.
</p><p>Social forces, such as <a href="/wiki/Feminization_of_poverty" title="Feminization of poverty">gender</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disability_and_poverty" title="Disability and poverty">disability</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Racial_inequality" title="Racial inequality">race and ethnicity</a>, can exacerbate issues of povertyâwith women, <a href="/wiki/Child_poverty" title="Child poverty">children</a> and minorities frequently bearing unequal burdens of poverty. Moreover, impoverished individuals are more vulnerable to the effects of other social issues, such as the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_justice" title="Environmental justice">environmental effects of industry</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_and_poverty" title="Climate change and poverty">impacts of climate change</a> or other <a href="/wiki/Natural_disaster" title="Natural disaster">natural disasters</a> or <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">extreme weather events</a>. Poverty can also make other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_problems" title="Social problems">social problems</a> worse; economic pressures on impoverished communities frequently play a part in <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Causes_of_biodiversity_loss" title="Causes of biodiversity loss">biodiversity loss</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_conflict" title="Ethnic conflict">ethnic conflict</a>. For this reason, the UN's <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a> and other international policy programs, such as the international recovery from COVID-19, emphasize the connection of poverty alleviation with other societal goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions_and_etymology">Definitions and etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Definitions and etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The word <i>poverty</i> comes from the old (Norman) French word <i>povertÃ©</i> (Modern French: <i>pauvretÃ©),</i> from Latin <i>paupertÄs</i> from <i>pauper</i> (poor).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are several definitions of poverty depending on the context of the situation it is placed in, and usually references a state or condition in which a person or community lacks the financial resources and essentials for a certain standard of living.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>: Fundamentally, poverty is a denial of choices and opportunities, a violation of human dignity. It means lack of basic capacity to participate effectively in society. It means not having enough to feed and clothe a family, not having a school or clinic to go to, not having the land on which to grow one's food or a job to earn one's living, not having access to credit. It means insecurity, powerlessness and exclusion of individuals, households and communities. It means susceptibility to violence, and it often implies living in marginal or fragile environments, without access to clean water or sanitation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>: Poverty is pronounced deprivation in well-being, and comprises many <a href="/wiki/Dimension" title="Dimension">dimensions</a>. It includes low incomes and the inability to acquire the basic goods and services necessary for <a href="/wiki/Survival_skills" title="Survival skills">survival</a> with dignity. Poverty also encompasses low levels of health and education, poor access to clean water and sanitation, inadequate physical security, lack of voice, and insufficient capacity and opportunity to better one's life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU): The European Union's definition of poverty is significantly different from definitions in other parts of the world, and consequently policy measures introduced to combat poverty in EU countries also differ from measures in other nations. Poverty is measured in relation to the distribution of income in each member country using relative income poverty lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-researchgate.net_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-researchgate.net-10">[10]</a></sup> Relative-income poverty rates in the EU are compiled by the <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>, in charge of coordinating, gathering, and disseminating member country <a href="/wiki/Statistics" title="Statistics">statistics</a> using <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> Survey of Income and Living Conditions (EU-SILC) surveys.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-researchgate.net_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-researchgate.net-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Measuring_poverty">Measuring poverty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Measuring poverty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Poverty_threshold" title="Poverty threshold">Poverty threshold</a> and <a href="/wiki/Individual_Deprivation_Measure" title="Individual Deprivation Measure">Individual Deprivation Measure</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DorotheaLangeMigrantWorkersChildren.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="11398" data-file-width="14750" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/DorotheaLangeMigrantWorkersChildren.jpg/220px-DorotheaLangeMigrantWorkersChildren.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/DorotheaLangeMigrantWorkersChildren.jpg/330px-DorotheaLangeMigrantWorkersChildren.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/DorotheaLangeMigrantWorkersChildren.jpg/440px-DorotheaLangeMigrantWorkersChildren.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DorotheaLangeMigrantWorkersChildren.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Children of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Depression</a>-era migrant workers, Arizona, United States, 1937</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Absolute_poverty">Absolute poverty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Absolute poverty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Extreme_poverty" title="Extreme poverty">Extreme poverty</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power" title="Purchasing power">Purchasing power</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asset_poverty" title="Asset poverty">Asset poverty</a></div>
<p>Absolute poverty, often synonymous with 'extreme poverty' or 'abject poverty', refers to a set standard which is consistent over time and between countries. This set standard usually refers to "a condition characterized by severe deprivation of basic human needs, including food, safe drinking water, sanitation facilities, health, shelter, education and information. It depends not only on income but also on access to services."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN1995_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN1995-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SachsEndofPoverty2005_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-SachsEndofPoverty2005-13">[13]</a></sup> Having an income below the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poverty_line" title="Poverty line">poverty line</a>, which is defined as an income needed to purchase basic needs, is also referred to as <i>primary proverty</i>.
</p><p>The "dollar a day" poverty line was first introduced in 1990 as a measure to meet such standards of living. For nations that do not use the US dollar as currency, "dollar a day" does not translate to living a day on the equivalent amount of local currency as determined by the <a href="/wiki/Exchange_rate" title="Exchange rate">exchange rate</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dollar_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-dollar-14">[14]</a></sup> Rather, it is determined by the <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> rate, which would look at how much local currency is needed to buy the same things that a dollar could buy in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dollar_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-dollar-14">[14]</a></sup> Usually, this would translate to having less local currency than if the exchange rate was used as the United States is a relatively more expensive country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dollar_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-dollar-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1993 through 2005, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> defined absolute poverty as $1.08 a day on such a <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> basis, after adjusting for inflation to the 1993 US dollar<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> and in 2008, it was updated as $1.25 a day (equivalent to $1.00 a day in 1996 US prices)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dollarrevisited2008_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-dollarrevisited2008-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RavaillionWB26Jun2009_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-RavaillionWB26Jun2009-17">[17]</a></sup> and in 2015, it was updated as living on less than US$1.90 per day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> and <i>moderate poverty</i> as less than $2 or $5 a day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Similarly, 'ultra-poverty' is defined by a 2007 report issued by International Food Policy Research Institute as living on less than 54 cents per day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The poverty line threshold of $1.90 per day, as set by the World Bank, is controversial. Each nation has its own threshold for absolute poverty line; in the United States, for example, the absolute poverty line was US$15.15 per day in 2010 (US$22,000 per year for a family of four),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> while in India it was US$1.0 per day<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wb2010a_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-wb2010a-22">[22]</a></sup> and in China the absolute poverty line was US$0.55 per day, each on PPP basis in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> These different poverty lines make data comparison between each nation's official reports qualitatively difficult. Some scholars argue that the World Bank method sets the bar too high, others argue it is too low.
</p><p>There is disagreement among experts as to what would be considered a realistic poverty rate with one considering it "an inaccurately measured and arbitrary cut off".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Some contend that a higher poverty line is needed, such as a minimum of $7.40 or even $10 to $15 a day. They argue that these levels would better reflect the cost of basic needs and normal life expectancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>One estimate places the true scale of poverty much higher than the World Bank, with an estimated 4.3 billion people (59% of the world's population) living with less than $5 a day and unable to meet basic needs adequately.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Philip_Alston" title="Philip Alston">Philip Alston</a>, a UN special rapporteur on extreme poverty and human rights, stated the World Bank's international poverty line of $1.90 a day is fundamentally flawed, and has allowed for "self congratulatory" triumphalism in the fight against extreme global poverty, which he asserts is "completely off track" and that nearly half of the global population, or 3.4 billion, lives on less than $5.50 a day, and this number has barely moved since 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Still others suggest that poverty line misleads as it measures everyone below the poverty line the same, when in reality someone living on $1.20 per day is in a different state of poverty than someone living on $0.20 per day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wb2010a_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-wb2010a-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other measures of absolute poverty without using a certain dollar amount include the standard defined as receiving less than 80% of minimum caloric intake whilst spending more than 80% of income on food, sometimes called ultra-poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relative_poverty">Relative poverty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Relative poverty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Relative_deprivation" title="Relative deprivation">Relative deprivation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">Economic inequality</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wealth_concentration" title="Wealth concentration">Wealth concentration</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Economics_Gini_coefficient2.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Economics_Gini_coefficient2.svg/220px-Economics_Gini_coefficient2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Economics_Gini_coefficient2.svg/330px-Economics_Gini_coefficient2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Economics_Gini_coefficient2.svg/440px-Economics_Gini_coefficient2.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Economics_Gini_coefficient2.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graphical representation of the <a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">Gini coefficient</a>, a common measure of inequality. The Gini coefficient is equal to the area marked <i>A</i> divided by the sum of the areas marked <i>A</i> and <i>B</i>, that is, <span class="nowrap">Gini = <i>A</i>/(<i>A</i> + <i>B</i>)</span>.</div></div></div>
<p>Relative poverty views poverty as socially defined and dependent on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_context" title="Social context">social context</a>. It is argued that the needs considered fundamental is not an objective measure<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Innocenti2012_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Innocenti2012-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rep1964_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-rep1964-32">[32]</a></sup> and could change with the custom of society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AdamSmith1776_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-AdamSmith1776-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Innocenti2012_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-Innocenti2012-31">[31]</a></sup> For example, a person who cannot afford housing better than a small tent in an open field would be said to live in relative poverty if almost everyone else in that area lives in modern brick homes, but not if everyone else also lives in small tents in open fields (for example, in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nomadic_tribe" title="Nomadic tribe">nomadic tribe</a>). Since richer nations would have lower levels of absolute poverty,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-relativeBradshawInnocenti2012_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-relativeBradshawInnocenti2012-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNICEF2000_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNICEF2000-35">[35]</a></sup> relative poverty is considered the "most useful measure for ascertaining poverty rates in wealthy developed nations"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raphael2009_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Raphael2009-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Innocenti2005_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Innocenti2005-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OECD2008_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-OECD2008-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNDP2008_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP2008-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ConferenceBoard2013_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-ConferenceBoard2013-40">[40]</a></sup> and is the "most prominent and most-quoted of the EU social inclusion indicators".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-povinequalityCSP_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-povinequalityCSP-41">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>Usually, relative poverty is measured as the percentage of the population with income less than some fixed proportion of median income. This is a calculation of the percentage of people whose family household income falls below the <a href="/wiki/Poverty_threshold" title="Poverty threshold">Poverty Line</a>. The main poverty line used in the OECD and the European Union is based on "economic distance", a level of income set at 60% of the median household income.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The United States federal government typically regulates this line to three times the cost of an adequate meal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are several other different <a href="/wiki/Income_inequality_metrics" title="Income inequality metrics">income inequality metrics</a>, for example, the <a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">Gini coefficient</a> or the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theil_Index" title="Theil Index">Theil Index</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Global_Wealth_Distribution_2020_(Property).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="444" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Global_Wealth_Distribution_2020_%28Property%29.svg/220px-Global_Wealth_Distribution_2020_%28Property%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Global_Wealth_Distribution_2020_%28Property%29.svg/330px-Global_Wealth_Distribution_2020_%28Property%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Global_Wealth_Distribution_2020_%28Property%29.svg/440px-Global_Wealth_Distribution_2020_%28Property%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Global_Wealth_Distribution_2020_(Property).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Global share of wealth by wealth group âCredit Suisse, 2021</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Global-share-of-wealth-by-wealth-group-768x409.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="351" data-file-width="735" decoding="async" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Global-share-of-wealth-by-wealth-group-768x409.png/220px-Global-share-of-wealth-by-wealth-group-768x409.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Global-share-of-wealth-by-wealth-group-768x409.png/330px-Global-share-of-wealth-by-wealth-group-768x409.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Global-share-of-wealth-by-wealth-group-768x409.png/440px-Global-share-of-wealth-by-wealth-group-768x409.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Global-share-of-wealth-by-wealth-group-768x409.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Global share of wealth by wealth group âCredit Suisse, 2017</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_aspects">Other aspects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Other aspects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rather than income, poverty is also measured through individual basic needs at a time. <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> has greatly increased in the developing world since World War II and is starting to close the gap to the developed world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Child_mortality" title="Child mortality">Child mortality</a> has decreased in every developing region of the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The proportion of the world's population living in countries where the daily per-capita supply of <a href="/wiki/Food_energy" title="Food energy">food energy</a> is less than 9,200 kilojoules (2,200 kilocalories) decreased from 56% in the mid-1960s to below 10% by the 1990s. Similar trends can be observed for literacy, access to clean water and electricity and basic consumer items.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tiggare_vid_Operak%C3%A4llaren.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1617" data-file-width="2312" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Tiggare_vid_Operak%C3%A4llaren.jpg/220px-Tiggare_vid_Operak%C3%A4llaren.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Tiggare_vid_Operak%C3%A4llaren.jpg/330px-Tiggare_vid_Operak%C3%A4llaren.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Tiggare_vid_Operak%C3%A4llaren.jpg/440px-Tiggare_vid_Operak%C3%A4llaren.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tiggare_vid_Operak%C3%A4llaren.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An early morning outside the Opera Tavern in Stockholm, with a gang of beggars waiting for delivery of the scraps from the previous day. <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, 1868.</div></div></div>
<p>Poverty may also be understood as an aspect of unequal <a href="/wiki/Social_status" title="Social status">social status</a> and inequitable social relationships, experienced as social exclusion, dependency, and diminished capacity to participate, or to develop meaningful connections with other people in society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Townsend1979_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Townsend1979-49">[49]</a></sup> Such social exclusion can be minimized through strengthened connections with the mainstream, such as through the provision of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relational_care" title="Relational care">relational care</a> to those who are experiencing poverty. The World Bank's "Voices of the Poor", based on research with over 20,000 poor people in 23 countries, identifies a range of factors which poor people identify as part of poverty. These include abuse by those in power, dis-empowering institutions, excluded locations, gender relationships, lack of security, limited capabilities, physical limitations, precarious livelihoods, problems in social relationships, weak community organizations and discrimination. Analysis of social aspects of poverty links conditions of scarcity to aspects of the distribution of resources and power in a society and recognizes that poverty may be a function of the diminished "capability" of people to live the kinds of lives they value. The social aspects of poverty may include lack of <a href="/wiki/Information_access" title="Information access">access to information</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Health_care" title="Health care">health care</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_capital" title="Social capital">social capital</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_power" title="Political power">political power</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Relational_poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Relational poverty (page does not exist)">Relational poverty</a> is the idea that societal poverty exists if there is a lack of human relationships. Relational poverty can be the result of a lost contact number, lack of phone ownership, isolation, or deliberate severing of ties with an individual or community. Relational poverty is also understood "by the social institutions that organize those relationships...poverty is importantly the result of the different terms and conditions on which people are included in social life"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Second_Cameron_ministry" title="Second Cameron ministry">second Cameron ministry</a> came under attack for their redefinition of poverty; poverty is no longer classified by a family's income, but as to whether a family is in work or not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian1_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian1-53">[53]</a></sup> Considering that two-thirds of people who found work were accepting wages that are below the living wage (according to the <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Rowntree_Foundation" title="Joseph Rowntree Foundation">Joseph Rowntree Foundation</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>) this has been criticised by anti-poverty campaigners as an unrealistic view of poverty in the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian1_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian1-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary_poverty">Secondary poverty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Secondary poverty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Secondary_poverty" title="Secondary poverty">Secondary poverty</a></div>
<p>Secondary poverty refers to those that earn enough income to not be impoverished, but who spend their income on unnecessary pleasures, such as <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage" title="Alcoholic beverage">alcoholic beverages</a>, thus placing them below it in practice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In 18th- and 19th-century <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>, the practice of <a href="/wiki/Temperance_movement" title="Temperance movement">temperance</a> among <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methodist" title="Methodist">Methodists</a>, as well as their rejection of <a href="/wiki/Gambling#Religious" title="Gambling">gambling</a>, allowed them to eliminate secondary poverty and accumulate capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Swatos1998_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Swatos1998-56">[56]</a></sup> Factors that contribute to secondary poverty includes but are not limited to: alcohol, gambling, tobacco and drugs.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Variability">Variability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Variability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Poverty levels are snapshot pictures in time that omits the transitional dynamics between levels. Mobility statistics supply additional information about the fraction who leave the poverty level. For example, one study finds that in a sixteen-year period (1975 to 1991 in the US) only 5% of those in the lower fifth of the income level were still at that level, while 95% transitioned to a higher income category.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Poverty levels can remain the same while those who rise out of poverty are replaced by others. The transient poor and chronic poor differ in each society. In a nine-year period ending in 2005 for the US, 50% of the poorest quintile transitioned to a higher quintile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_prevalence">Global prevalence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Global prevalence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_percentage_of_population_living_in_poverty" title="List of countries by percentage of population living in poverty">List of countries by percentage of population living in poverty</a></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Worlds_regions_by_total_wealth(in_trillions_USD),_2018.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1334" data-file-width="1889" decoding="async" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Worlds_regions_by_total_wealth%28in_trillions_USD%29%2C_2018.jpg/250px-Worlds_regions_by_total_wealth%28in_trillions_USD%29%2C_2018.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Worlds_regions_by_total_wealth%28in_trillions_USD%29%2C_2018.jpg/375px-Worlds_regions_by_total_wealth%28in_trillions_USD%29%2C_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Worlds_regions_by_total_wealth%28in_trillions_USD%29%2C_2018.jpg/500px-Worlds_regions_by_total_wealth%28in_trillions_USD%29%2C_2018.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Worlds_regions_by_total_wealth(in_trillions_USD),_2018.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Worlds regions by total wealth (in trillions USD), 2018</div></div></div>
<p>According to Chen and Ravallion, about 1.76 billion people in developing world lived <i>above</i> $1.25 per day and 1.9 billion people lived <i>below</i> $1.25 per day in 1981. In 2005, about 4.09 billion people in developing world lived above $1.25 per day and 1.4 billion people lived below $1.25 per day (both 1981 and 2005 data are on inflation adjusted basis).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The share of the world's population living in absolute poverty fell from 43% in 1981 to 14% in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldbank-Poverty_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank-Poverty-61">[61]</a></sup> The absolute number of people in poverty fell from 1.95 billion in 1981 to 1.01 billion in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PovertyRoser_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-PovertyRoser-62">[62]</a></sup> The economist <a href="/wiki/Max_Roser" title="Max Roser">Max Roser</a> estimates that the number of people in poverty is therefore roughly the same as 200 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PovertyRoser_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-PovertyRoser-62">[62]</a></sup> This is the case since the world population was just little more than 1 billion in 1820 and the majority (84% to 94%)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> of the world population was living in poverty. The proportion of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_world" title="Developing world">developing world</a>'s population living in extreme economic poverty fell from 28% in 1990 to 21% in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldbank-Poverty_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank-Poverty-61">[61]</a></sup> Most of this improvement has occurred in <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1980s_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-1980s-64">[64]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012 it was estimated that, using a poverty line of $1.25 a day, 1.2 billion people lived in poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Given the current economic model, built on <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>, it would take 100 years to bring the world's poorest up to the poverty line of $1.25 a day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> estimates half the world's children (or 1.1 billion) live in poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The World Bank forecasted in 2015 that <a href="/wiki/Global_Monitoring_Report_(World_Bank)" title="Global Monitoring Report (World Bank)">702.1 million people</a> were living in extreme poverty, down from 1.75 billion in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Extreme poverty is observed in all parts of the world, including developed economies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Of the 2015 population, about 347.1 million people (35.2%) lived in <a href="/wiki/Global_Monitoring_Report_(World_Bank)" title="Global Monitoring Report (World Bank)">Sub-Saharan Africa</a> and 231.3 million (13.5%) lived in <a href="/wiki/Global_Monitoring_Report_(World_Bank)" title="Global Monitoring Report (World Bank)">South Asia</a>. According to the World Bank, between 1990 and 2015, the percentage of the world's population living in extreme poverty fell from 37.1% to 9.6%, falling below 10% for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> During the 2013 to 2015 period, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank</a> reported that extreme poverty fell from 11% to 10%, however they also noted that the rate of decline had slowed by nearly half from the 25 year average with parts of sub-saharan Africa returning to early 2000 levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The World Bank attributed this to increasing violence following the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a>, <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">population increases</a> in Sub-Saharan Africa, and general African inflationary pressures and economic malaise were the primary drivers for this slow down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Many wealthy nations have seen an increase in relative poverty rates ever since the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a>, in particular among children from impoverished families who often reside in substandard housing and find educational opportunities out of reach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> It has been argued by some academics that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neoliberal" title="Neoliberal">neoliberal</a> policies promoted by global financial institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a> and the World Bank are actually exacerbating both inequality and poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>In East Asia the World Bank reported that "The poverty headcount rate at the $2-a-day level is estimated to have fallen to about 27 percent [in 2007], down from 29.5 percent in 2006 and 69 percent in 1990."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>  The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a> accounts for over three quarters of global poverty reduction from 1990 to 2005. China accounted for nearly half of all <a href="/wiki/Extreme_poverty" title="Extreme poverty">extreme poverty</a> in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Sub-Saharan Africa extreme poverty went up from 41% in 1981 to 46% in 2001,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> which combined with growing population increased the number of people living in extreme poverty from 231 million to 318 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-birthrates_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-birthrates-82">[82]</a></sup> Statistics of 2018 shows population living in extreme conditions has declined by more than 1 billion in the last 25 years. As per the report published by the world bank on 19 September 2018 world poverty falls below 750 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the early 1990s some of the transition economies of Central and Eastern Europe and Central Asia experienced a sharp drop in income.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collapse_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Collapse of the Soviet Union">collapse of the Soviet Union</a> resulted in large declines in GDP per capita, of about 30 to 35% between 1990 and the through year of 1998 (when it was at its minimum). As a result, poverty rates tripled,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> excess mortality increased,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> and life expectancy declined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> By 1999, during the peak of the poverty crisis, 191 million people were living on less than $5.50 a day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GhodseeOrenstein_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-GhodseeOrenstein-88">[88]</a></sup> In subsequent years as per capita incomes recovered the poverty rate dropped from 31.4% of the population to 19.6%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Soviet_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Soviet-90">[90]</a></sup> The average post-communist country had returned to 1989 levels of per-capita GDP by 2005,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> although as of 2015 some are still far behind that.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> According to the World Bank in 2014, around 80 million people were still living on less than $5.00 a day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GhodseeOrenstein_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-GhodseeOrenstein-88">[88]</a></sup>
</p><p>World Bank data shows that the percentage of the population living in households with consumption or income per person below the poverty line has decreased in each region of the world except Middle East and North Africa since 1990:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Characteristics">Characteristics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Characteristics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Life_expectancy_1950-2005.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="632" data-file-width="910" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Life_expectancy_1950-2005.png/220px-Life_expectancy_1950-2005.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Life_expectancy_1950-2005.png/330px-Life_expectancy_1950-2005.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Life_expectancy_1950-2005.png/440px-Life_expectancy_1950-2005.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Life_expectancy_1950-2005.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Life expectancy has been increasing and converging for most of the world. Sub-Saharan Africa has recently seen a decline, partly related to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS_epidemic" title="AIDS epidemic">AIDS epidemic</a>. Graph shows the years 1950â2005.</div></div></div><p>
The effects of poverty may also be causes as listed above, thus creating a "poverty cycle" operating across multiple levels, individual, local, national and global.</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VOA_Heinlein_-_Somali_refugees_September_2011_-_09.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="535" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/VOA_Heinlein_-_Somali_refugees_September_2011_-_09.jpg/220px-VOA_Heinlein_-_Somali_refugees_September_2011_-_09.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/VOA_Heinlein_-_Somali_refugees_September_2011_-_09.jpg/330px-VOA_Heinlein_-_Somali_refugees_September_2011_-_09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/VOA_Heinlein_-_Somali_refugees_September_2011_-_09.jpg/440px-VOA_Heinlein_-_Somali_refugees_September_2011_-_09.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VOA_Heinlein_-_Somali_refugees_September_2011_-_09.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_and_humanitarian_efforts_in_the_Somali_Civil_War" title="Diplomatic and humanitarian efforts in the Somali Civil War">Somali</a> boy receiving treatment for malnourishment at a health facility</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Diseases_of_poverty" title="Diseases of poverty">Diseases of poverty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Disability_and_poverty" title="Disability and poverty">Disability and poverty</a></div>
<p>One-third of deaths around the worldâsome 18 million people a year or 50,000 per dayâare due to poverty-related causes. People living in developing nations, among them women and children, are over represented among the global poor and these effects of severe poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Those living in poverty suffer disproportionately from hunger or even <a href="/wiki/Starvation" title="Starvation">starvation</a> and disease, as well as lower <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hunger" title="Hunger">hunger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a> are the single gravest threats to the world's public health and malnutrition is by far the biggest contributor to <a href="/wiki/Child_mortality" title="Child mortality">child mortality</a>, present in half of all cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economist_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-economist-102">[102]</a></sup>
</p><p>Almost 90% of <a href="/wiki/Maternal_death" title="Maternal death">maternal deaths</a> during childbirth occur in Asia and sub-Saharan Africa, compared to less than 1% in the developed world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Those who live in poverty have also been shown to have a far greater likelihood of having or incurring a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disability_and_Poverty" title="Disability and Poverty">disability</a> within their lifetime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infectious_diseases" title="Infectious diseases">Infectious diseases</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> can perpetuate poverty by diverting health and economic resources from investment and productivity; malaria decreases GDP growth by up to 1.3% in some <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing nations</a> and AIDS decreases African growth by 0.3â1.5% annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup>
</p><p>Studies have shown that poverty impedes cognitive function although some of these findings could not be replicated in follow-up studies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> One hypothesised mechanism is that financial worries put a severe burden on one's mental resources so that they are no longer fully available for solving complicated problems. The reduced capability for problem solving can lead to suboptimal decisions and further perpetuate poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Many other pathways from poverty to compromised cognitive capacities have been noted, from poor nutrition and environmental toxins to the effects of stress on parenting behavior, all of which lead to suboptimal psychological development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Neuroscientists have documented the impact of poverty on brain structure and function throughout the lifespan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup>
</p><p>Infectious diseases continue to blight the lives of the poor across the world. 36.8 million people are living with HIV/AIDS, with 954,492 deaths in 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup>
</p><p>Poor people often are more prone to severe diseases due to the lack of health care, and due to living in non-optimal conditions. Among the poor, girls tend to suffer even more due to gender discrimination. Economic stability is paramount in a poor household; otherwise they go in an endless loop of negative income trying to treat diseases. Often when a person in a poor household falls ill it is up to the family members to take care of them due to limited access to health care and lack of health insurance. The household members often have to give up their income or stop seeking further education to tend to the sick member. There is a greater opportunity cost imposed on the poor to tend to someone compared to someone with better financial stability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Substance_abuse" title="Substance abuse">Substance abuse</a> means that the poor typically spend about 2% of their income educating their children but larger percentages of alcohol and tobacco (for example, 6% in Indonesia and 8% in Mexico).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hunger">Hunger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Hunger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hunger" title="Hunger">Hunger</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">Malnutrition</a></div>
<p>Rises in the costs of living make poor people less able to afford items. Poor people spend a <a href="/wiki/Engel%27s_law" title="Engel's law">greater portion of their budgets</a> on food than wealthy people. As a result, poor households and those near the poverty threshold can be particularly vulnerable to increases in <a href="/wiki/Food_prices" title="Food prices">food prices</a>. For example, in late 2007 increases in the price of grains<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> led to <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%932008_world_food_price_crisis" title="2007â2008 world food price crisis">food riots</a> in some countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> warned that 100 million people were at risk of sinking deeper into poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Threats to the supply of food may also be caused by drought and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_crisis" title="Water crisis">water crisis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Intensive_farming" title="Intensive farming">Intensive farming</a> often leads to a vicious cycle of exhaustion of <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">soil fertility</a> and decline of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agricultural_yields" title="Agricultural yields">agricultural yields</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Approximately 40% of the world's <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_land" title="Agricultural land">agricultural land</a> is seriously degraded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_Africa" title="Poverty in Africa">Africa</a>, if current trends of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soil_degradation" title="Soil degradation">soil degradation</a> continue, the continent might be able to feed just 25% of its population by 2025, according to <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_University" title="United Nations University">United Nations University</a>'s Ghana-based Institute for Natural Resources in Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Every year nearly 11 million children living in poverty die before their fifth birthday. 1.02 billion people go to bed hungry every night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Global_Hunger_Index" title="Global Hunger Index">Global Hunger Index</a>, Sub-Saharan Africa had the highest child malnutrition rate of the world's regions over the 2001â2006 period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ghi2008_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-ghi2008-127">[127]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mental_health">Mental health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Mental health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Venezuelan_eating_from_garbage.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1615" data-file-width="2880" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Venezuelan_eating_from_garbage.jpg/250px-Venezuelan_eating_from_garbage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Venezuelan_eating_from_garbage.jpg/375px-Venezuelan_eating_from_garbage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Venezuelan_eating_from_garbage.jpg/500px-Venezuelan_eating_from_garbage.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Venezuelan_eating_from_garbage.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Venezuelan eating from garbage during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crisis_in_Bolivarian_Venezuela" title="Crisis in Bolivarian Venezuela">crisis in Bolivarian Venezuela</a></div></div></div>
<p>A psychological study has been conducted by four scientists during inaugural Convention of Psychological Science. The results find that people who thrive with financial stability or fall under low socioeconomic status (SES) tend to perform worse cognitively due to external pressure imposed upon them. The research found that stressors such as low income, inadequate health care, discrimination, and exposure to criminal activities all contribute to mental disorders. This study also found that children exposed to poverty-stricken environments have slower cognitive thinking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> It is seen that children perform better under the care of their parents and that children tend to adopt speaking language at a younger age. Since being in poverty from childhood is more harmful than it is for an adult, it is seen that children in poor households tend to fall behind in certain cognitive abilities compared to other average families.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup>
</p><p>For a child to grow up emotionally healthy, the children under three need "A strong, reliable primary caregiver who provides consistent and unconditional love, guidance, and support. Safe, predictable, stable environments. Ten to 20 hours each week of harmonious, reciprocal interactions. This process, known as attunement, is most crucial during the first 6â24 months of infants' lives and helps them develop a wider range of healthy emotions, including gratitude, forgiveness, and empathy. Enrichment through personalized, increasingly complex activities".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In one survey, 67% of children from disadvantaged <a href="/wiki/Inner_city" title="Inner city">inner cities</a> said they had witnessed a serious assault, and 33% reported witnessing a homicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> 51% of fifth graders from <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a> (median income for a household: $27,133) have been found to be victims of violence, compared to 32% in Washington, DC (mean income for a household: $40,127).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Studies have shown that poverty changes the personalities of children who live in it. The <a href="/wiki/Great_Smoky_Mountains_Study" title="Great Smoky Mountains Study">Great Smoky Mountains Study</a> was a ten-year study that was able to demonstrate this. During the study, about one-quarter of the families saw a dramatic and unexpected increase in income. The study showed that among these children, instances of behavioral and emotional disorders decreased, and conscientiousness and agreeableness increased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MyUser_The_Washington_Post_October_8_2015c_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-MyUser_The_Washington_Post_October_8_2015c-132">[132]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Social_determinants_of_health_in_poverty#Education" title="Social determinants of health in poverty">Social determinants of health in poverty Â§Â Education</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Disability_and_poverty#Education" title="Disability and poverty">Disability and poverty Â§Â Education</a></div>
<p>Research has found that there is a high risk of educational underachievement for children who are from low-income housing circumstances. This is often a process that begins in primary school. Instruction in the US educational system, as well as in most other countries, tends to be geared towards those students who come from more advantaged backgrounds. As a result, children in poverty are at a higher risk than advantaged children for retention in their grade, special deleterious placements during the school's hours and not completing their high school education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SYF_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-SYF-133">[133]</a></sup> Advantage breeds advantage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> There are many explanations for why students tend to drop out of school. One is the conditions in which they attend school. Schools in poverty-stricken areas have conditions that hinder children from learning in a safe environment. Researchers have developed a name for areas like this: an <i>urban war zone</i> is a poor, crime-laden district in which deteriorated, violent, even warlike conditions and underfunded, largely ineffective schools promote inferior academic performance, including irregular attendance and disruptive or non-compliant classroom behavior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> Because of poverty, "Students from low-income families are 2.4 times more likely to drop out than middle-income kids, and over 10 times more likely than high-income peers to drop out."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup>
</p><p>For children with low resources, the risk factors are similar to others such as <a href="/wiki/Juvenile_delinquency" title="Juvenile delinquency">juvenile delinquency</a> rates, higher levels of <a href="/wiki/Teenage_pregnancy" title="Teenage pregnancy">teenage pregnancy</a>, and economic dependency upon their low-income parent or parents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SYF_133-1"><a href="#cite_note-SYF-133">[133]</a></sup>
Families and society who submit low levels of investment in the education and development of less fortunate children end up with less favorable results for the children who see a life of parental employment reduction and low wages. Higher rates of early childbearing with all the connected risks to family, health and well-being are major issues to address since education from preschool to high school is identifiably meaningful in a life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SYF_133-2"><a href="#cite_note-SYF-133">[133]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Situation_Analysis_of_Out-of-School_Children_in_Nine_Southeast_Asian_Countries.pdf"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1752" data-file-width="1239" decoding="async" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Situation_Analysis_of_Out-of-School_Children_in_Nine_Southeast_Asian_Countries.pdf/page1-220px-Situation_Analysis_of_Out-of-School_Children_in_Nine_Southeast_Asian_Countries.pdf.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Situation_Analysis_of_Out-of-School_Children_in_Nine_Southeast_Asian_Countries.pdf/page1-330px-Situation_Analysis_of_Out-of-School_Children_in_Nine_Southeast_Asian_Countries.pdf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Situation_Analysis_of_Out-of-School_Children_in_Nine_Southeast_Asian_Countries.pdf/page1-440px-Situation_Analysis_of_Out-of-School_Children_in_Nine_Southeast_Asian_Countries.pdf.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Situation_Analysis_of_Out-of-School_Children_in_Nine_Southeast_Asian_Countries.pdf" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Out of school child</div></div></div>
<p>Poverty often drastically affects children's success in school. A child's "home activities, preferences, mannerisms" must align with the world and in the cases that they do not do these, students are at a disadvantage in the school and, most importantly, the classroom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANF_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-ANF-137">[137]</a></sup> Therefore, it is safe to state that children who live at or below the poverty level will have far less success educationally than children who live above the poverty line. Poor children have a great deal less healthcare and this ultimately results in many absences from school. Additionally, poor children are much more likely to suffer from hunger, fatigue, irritability, headaches, ear infections, flu, and colds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANF_137-1"><a href="#cite_note-ANF-137">[137]</a></sup> These illnesses could potentially restrict a student's focus and concentration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup>
</p><p>In general, the interaction of <a href="/wiki/Gender" title="Gender">gender</a> with poverty or location tends to work to the disadvantage of <a href="/wiki/Girl" title="Girl">girls</a> in poorer countries with low completion rates and social expectations that they marry early, and to the disadvantage of <a href="/wiki/Boy" title="Boy">boys</a> in richer countries with high completion rates but social expectations that they enter the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labour_force" title="Labour force">labour force</a> early.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-139">[139]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Primary_education" title="Primary education">primary education</a> level, most countries with a completion rate below 60% exhibit <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gender_disparity" title="Gender disparity">gender disparity</a> at girls' expense, particularly poor and rural girls. In Mauritania, the adjusted gender parity index is 0.86 on average, but only 0.63 for the poorest 20%, while there is parity among the richest 20%. In countries with completion rates between 60% and 80%, gender disparity is generally smaller, but disparity at the expense of poor girls is especially marked in <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>. Exceptions in the opposite direction are observed in countries with pastoralist economies that rely on boys' labour, such as the <a href="/wiki/Eswatini" title="Eswatini">Kingdom of Eswatini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a> and <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_139-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-139">[139]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shelter">Shelter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Shelter">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slums" title="Slums">Slums</a>, <a href="/wiki/Street_children" title="Street children">Street children</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orphanages" title="Orphanages">Orphanages</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gentrification" title="Gentrification">Gentrification</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kolkata_(4131122903).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Kolkata_%284131122903%29.jpg/220px-Kolkata_%284131122903%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Kolkata_%284131122903%29.jpg/330px-Kolkata_%284131122903%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Kolkata_%284131122903%29.jpg/440px-Kolkata_%284131122903%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kolkata_(4131122903).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Homeless family in Kolkata, India</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Street_Child,_Srimangal_Railway_Station.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1565" data-file-width="2516" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Street_Child%2C_Srimangal_Railway_Station.jpg/220px-Street_Child%2C_Srimangal_Railway_Station.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Street_Child%2C_Srimangal_Railway_Station.jpg/330px-Street_Child%2C_Srimangal_Railway_Station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Street_Child%2C_Srimangal_Railway_Station.jpg/440px-Street_Child%2C_Srimangal_Railway_Station.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Street_Child,_Srimangal_Railway_Station.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Street child in <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>. Aiding relatives financially unable to but willing to take in orphans is found to be more effective by cost and welfare than orphanages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-orphanages_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-orphanages-140">[140]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The geographic concentration of poverty is argued to be a factor in entrenching poverty. William J. Wilson's "concentration and isolation" hypothesis states that the economic difficulties of the very poorest African Americans are compounded by the fact that as the better-off African Americans move out, the poorest are more and more concentrated, having only other very poor people as neighbors. This concentration causes social isolation, Wilson suggests, because the very poor are now isolated from access to the job networks, role models, institutions, and other connections that might help them escape poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gentrification" title="Gentrification">Gentrification</a> means converting an aging neighborhood into a more affluent one, as by remodeling homes. Landlords then increase rent on newly renovated real estate; the poor people cannot afford to pay high rent, and may need to leave their neighborhood to find affordable housing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> The poor also get more access to income and services, while studies suggest poor residents living in gentrifying neighbourhoods are actually less likely to move than poor residents of non-gentrifying areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p>
Poverty increases the risk of <a href="/wiki/Homelessness" title="Homelessness">homelessness</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> Slum-dwellers, who make up a third of the world's urban population, live in a poverty no better, if not worse, than rural people, who are the traditional focus of the poverty in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_world" title="Developing world">developing world</a>, according to a report by the United Nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tallinn_lower_town,_May_1996.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1341" data-file-width="980" decoding="async" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Tallinn_lower_town%2C_May_1996.jpg/170px-Tallinn_lower_town%2C_May_1996.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Tallinn_lower_town%2C_May_1996.jpg/255px-Tallinn_lower_town%2C_May_1996.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Tallinn_lower_town%2C_May_1996.jpg/340px-Tallinn_lower_town%2C_May_1996.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tallinn_lower_town,_May_1996.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dilapidated alley and buildings at the lower town of <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">Tallinn</a> in May 1996</div></div></div><p>There are over 100 million <a href="/wiki/Street_children" title="Street children">street children</a> worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Most of the children living in institutions around the world have a surviving parent or close relative, and they most commonly entered orphanages because of poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-orphanages_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-orphanages-140">[140]</a></sup> It is speculated that, flush with money, for-profit orphanages are increasing and push for children to join even though demographic data show that even the poorest extended families usually take in children whose parents have died.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-orphanages_140-2"><a href="#cite_note-orphanages-140">[140]</a></sup> Many child advocates maintain that this can harm children's <a href="/wiki/Child_development" title="Child development">development</a> by separating them from their families and that it would be more effective and cheaper to aid close relatives who want to take in the orphans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-orphanages_140-3"><a href="#cite_note-orphanages-140">[140]</a></sup>
</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Utilities">Utilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Utilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toilet_at_a_Village_near_Jaipur_installed_by_Pronto_Panels.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="2448" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Toilet_at_a_Village_near_Jaipur_installed_by_Pronto_Panels.JPG/150px-Toilet_at_a_Village_near_Jaipur_installed_by_Pronto_Panels.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Toilet_at_a_Village_near_Jaipur_installed_by_Pronto_Panels.JPG/225px-Toilet_at_a_Village_near_Jaipur_installed_by_Pronto_Panels.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Toilet_at_a_Village_near_Jaipur_installed_by_Pronto_Panels.JPG/300px-Toilet_at_a_Village_near_Jaipur_installed_by_Pronto_Panels.JPG 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toilet_at_a_Village_near_Jaipur_installed_by_Pronto_Panels.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Affordable household toilets near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaipur,_Rajasthan" title="Jaipur, Rajasthan">Jaipur, Rajasthan</a></div></div></div>
