<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_and_sanitation">Water and sanitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Water and sanitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>As of 2012, 2.5 billion people lack access to sanitation services and 15% practice <a href="/wiki/Open_defecation" title="Open defecation">open defecation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> The most noteworthy example is Bangladesh, which had half the GDP per capita of India but has a lower mortality from diarrhea than India or the world average, with diarrhea deaths declining by 90% since the 1990s. Even while providing latrines is a challenge, people still do not use them even when available. By strategically providing pit latrines to the poorest, charities in Bangladesh sparked a cultural change as those better off perceived it as an issue of status to not use one. The vast majority of the latrines built were then not from charities but by villagers themselves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup>
</p><p>Water utility subsidies tend to subsidize water consumption by those connected to the supply grid, which is typically skewed towards the richer and urban segment of the population and those outside informal housing. As a result of heavy consumption subsidies, the price of water decreases to the extent that only 30%, on average, of the supplying costs in developing countries is covered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kenny_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kenny-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-utilitysubsidy_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-utilitysubsidy-150">[150]</a></sup>
This results in a lack of incentive to maintain delivery systems, leading to losses from leaks annually that are enough for 200 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kenny_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kenny-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup>
This also leads to a lack of incentive to invest in expanding the network, resulting in much of the poor population being unconnected to the network. Instead, the poor buy water from water vendors for, on average, about 5 to 16 times the metered price.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kenny_149-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kenny-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> However, subsidies for laying new connections to the network rather than for consumption have shown more promise for the poor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-utilitysubsidy_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-utilitysubsidy-150">[150]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="excerpt-block"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066933788">.mw-parser-output .excerpt-hat .mw-editsection-like{font-style:normal}</style><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Energy_poverty" title="Energy poverty">Energy poverty</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Energy_poverty&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:345px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HFHI_GVDC_Poverty_Housing.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="257" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/HFHI_GVDC_Poverty_Housing.JPG/343px-HFHI_GVDC_Poverty_Housing.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/HFHI_GVDC_Poverty_Housing.JPG/515px-HFHI_GVDC_Poverty_Housing.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/HFHI_GVDC_Poverty_Housing.JPG/686px-HFHI_GVDC_Poverty_Housing.JPG 2x" width="343"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HFHI_GVDC_Poverty_Housing.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Homes without reliable access to energy such as electricity, heating, cooling, etc.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Energy_poverty" title="Energy poverty">Energy poverty</a> is lack of access to modern energy services. It refers to the situation of large numbers of people in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_countries" title="Developing countries">developing countries</a> and some people in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developed_countries" title="Developed countries">developed countries</a> whose well-being is negatively affected by very low consumption of <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">energy</a>, use of dirty or polluting fuels, and excessive time spent collecting fuel to meet basic needs. Today, 759 million people lack access to consistent electricity and 2.6 billion people use dangerous and inefficient cooking systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Energy_poverty_:2_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-Energy_poverty_:2-153">[153]</a></sup> It is inversely related to access to modern energy services, although improving access is only one factor in efforts to reduce energy poverty. Energy poverty is distinct from <a href="/wiki/Fuel_poverty" title="Fuel poverty">fuel poverty</a>, which primarily focuses solely on the issue of affordability.
</p><p>The term âenergy povertyâ came into emergence through the publication of <a href="/wiki/Brenda_Boardman" title="Brenda Boardman">Brenda Boardman</a>âs book, <i>Fuel Poverty: From Cold Homes to Affordable Warmth</i> (1991). Naming the intersection of energy and poverty as âenergy povertyâ motivated the need to develop public policy to address energy poverty and also study its causes, symptoms, and effects in society. When energy poverty was first introduced in Boardman's book, energy poverty was described as not having enough power to heat and cool homes. Today, energy poverty is understood to be the result of complex systemic inequalities which create barriers to access modern energy at an affordable price. Energy poverty is challenging to measure and thus analyze because it is privately experienced within households, specific to cultural contexts, and dynamically changes depending on the time and space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup>
</p>
According to the Energy Poverty Action initiative of the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a>, "Access to energy is fundamental to improving quality of life and is a key imperative for economic development. In the developing world, energy poverty is still rife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup>". As a result of this situation, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (UN) launched the <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Energy_for_All" title="Sustainable Energy for All">Sustainable Energy for All Initiative</a> and designated 2012 as the <i>International Year for Sustainable Energy for All</i>, which had a major focus on reducing energy poverty. The UN further recognizes the importance of energy poverty through Goal 7 of its Sustainable Development Goals to "ensure access to affordable, reliable, sustainable, and modern energy for all."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Energy_poverty_:2_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-Energy_poverty_:2-153">[153]</a></sup></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prejudice_and_exploitation">Prejudice and exploitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Prejudice and exploitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oxfam_East_Africa_-_SomalilandDrought022.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4288" data-file-width="2848" decoding="async" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Oxfam_East_Africa_-_SomalilandDrought022.jpg/150px-Oxfam_East_Africa_-_SomalilandDrought022.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Oxfam_East_Africa_-_SomalilandDrought022.jpg/225px-Oxfam_East_Africa_-_SomalilandDrought022.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Oxfam_East_Africa_-_SomalilandDrought022.jpg/300px-Oxfam_East_Africa_-_SomalilandDrought022.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oxfam_East_Africa_-_SomalilandDrought022.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The urban poor buy water from water vendors for, on average, about 5 to 16 times the metered price.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kenny_149-3"><a href="#cite_note-Kenny-149">[149]</a></sup></div></div></div><p>Cultural factors, such as discrimination of various kinds, can negatively affect productivity such as <a href="/wiki/Ageism" title="Ageism">age discrimination</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stereotype" title="Stereotype">stereotyping</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> discrimination against people with physical disability,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disabpov_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-disabpov-157">[157]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sexism" title="Sexism">gender discrimination</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racial discrimination</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Caste" title="Caste">caste discrimination</a>. <a href="/wiki/Child_poverty" title="Child poverty">Children</a> are more than twice as likely to live in poverty as adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> Women are the group suffering from the highest rate of poverty after children, in what is referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Feminization_of_poverty" title="Feminization of poverty">feminization of poverty</a>. In addition, the fact that women are more likely to be caregivers, regardless of income level, to either the generations before or after them, exacerbates the burdens of their poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Those in poverty have increased chances of incurring a disability which leads to a cycle where <a href="/wiki/Disability_and_poverty" title="Disability and poverty">disability and poverty</a> are mutually reinforcing.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Max_Weber" title="Max Weber">Max Weber</a> and some schools of <a href="/wiki/Modernization_theory" title="Modernization theory">modernization theory</a> suggest that cultural <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Value_(personal_and_cultural)" title="Value (personal and cultural)">values</a> could affect economic success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> However, researchers<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (November 2009)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> have gathered evidence that suggest that values are not as deeply ingrained and that changing economic opportunities explain most of the movement into and out of poverty, as opposed to shifts in values.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kerbo2006a_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-kerbo2006a-162">[162]</a></sup> A 2018 report on poverty in the United States by UN special rapporteur <a href="/wiki/Philip_Alston" title="Philip Alston">Philip Alston</a> asserts that caricatured narratives about the rich and the poor (that "the rich are industrious, entrepreneurial, patriotic and the drivers of economic success" while "the poor are wasters, losers and scammers") are largely inaccurate, as "the poor are overwhelmingly those born into poverty, or those thrust there by circumstances largely beyond their control, such as physical or mental disabilities, divorce, family breakdown, illness, old age, unlivable wages or discrimination in the job market."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> Societal perception of people experiencing economic difficulty has historically appeared as a conceptual dichotomy: the "good" poor (people who are physically impaired, disabled, the "ill and incurable," the elderly, pregnant women, children) vs. the "bad" poor (able-bodied, "valid" adults, most often male).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to experts, many women become victims of trafficking, the most common form of which is <a href="/wiki/Survival_sex" title="Survival sex">prostitution</a>, as a means of survival and economic desperation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> Deterioration of living conditions can often compel children to abandon school to contribute to the family income, putting them at risk of being exploited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> For example, in <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>, a number of girls are turning to sex in return for food to survive because of the increasing poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> According to studies, as poverty decreases there will be fewer and fewer instances of violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Poverty_reduction">Poverty reduction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Poverty reduction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Poverty_reduction" title="Poverty reduction">Poverty reduction</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Aid" title="Aid">Aid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Development_aid" title="Development aid">Development aid</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sustainable_Development_Goal_01NoPoverty.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="139" data-file-width="139" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Sustainable_Development_Goal_01NoPoverty.svg/220px-Sustainable_Development_Goal_01NoPoverty.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Sustainable_Development_Goal_01NoPoverty.svg/330px-Sustainable_Development_Goal_01NoPoverty.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Sustainable_Development_Goal_01NoPoverty.svg/440px-Sustainable_Development_Goal_01NoPoverty.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sustainable_Development_Goal_01NoPoverty.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Logo of the <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_1" title="Sustainable Development Goal 1">Sustainable Development Goal 1</a> of the United Nations, to "end poverty in all its forms, everywhere" by 2030<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:172_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-:172-169">[169]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Various poverty reduction strategies are broadly categorized based on whether they make more of the basic human needs available or whether they increase the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disposable_income" title="Disposable income">disposable income</a> needed to purchase those needs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> Some strategies such as building roads can both bring access to various basic needs, such as fertilizer or healthcare from urban areas, as well as increase incomes, by bringing better access to urban markets.
</p><p>In 2015 all UN Member States adopted the 17 <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a> as part of the 2030 Agenda for sustainable development. <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_1" title="Sustainable Development Goal 1">Goal 1</a> is to "end poverty in all its forms everywhere".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> It aims to eliminate extreme poverty for all people measured by daily wages less than $1.25 and at least half the total number of men, women, and children living in poverty. In addition, social protection systems must be established at the national level and equal access to economic resources must be ensured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> Strategies have to be developed at the national, regional and international levels to support the eradication of poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Increasing_the_supply_of_basic_needs">Increasing the supply of basic needs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Increasing the supply of basic needs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_and_other_goods">Food and other goods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Food and other goods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spraying_Oilseed_Rape_near_Barton_Grange_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1842382.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="428" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Spraying_Oilseed_Rape_near_Barton_Grange_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1842382.jpg/220px-Spraying_Oilseed_Rape_near_Barton_Grange_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1842382.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Spraying_Oilseed_Rape_near_Barton_Grange_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1842382.jpg/330px-Spraying_Oilseed_Rape_near_Barton_Grange_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1842382.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Spraying_Oilseed_Rape_near_Barton_Grange_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1842382.jpg/440px-Spraying_Oilseed_Rape_near_Barton_Grange_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1842382.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spraying_Oilseed_Rape_near_Barton_Grange_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1842382.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spreading <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">fertilizer</a> on a field of <a href="/wiki/Rapeseed" title="Rapeseed">Rapeseed</a> near <a href="/wiki/Barton-upon-Humber" title="Barton-upon-Humber">Barton-upon-Humber</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a></div></div></div>
<p>Agricultural technologies such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nitrogen_fertilizer" title="Nitrogen fertilizer">nitrogen fertilizers</a>, pesticides, new seed varieties and new irrigation methods have dramatically reduced food shortages in modern times by boosting yields past previous constraints.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> Goal 2 of the <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a> is the elimination of hunger and undernutrition by 2030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup>
</p><p>Before the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, poverty had been mostly accepted as inevitable as economies produced little, making wealth scarce.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-176">[176]</a></sup> Geoffrey Parker wrote that "In <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a>, two of the largest cities in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">western Europe</a>, by 1600 three-quarters of the total population were too poor to pay taxes, and therefore likely to need relief in times of crisis."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> The initial industrial revolution led to high economic growth and eliminated mass absolute poverty in what is now considered the developed world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-178">[178]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mass_production" title="Mass production">Mass production</a> of goods in places such as rapidly industrializing China has made what were once considered luxuries, such as vehicles and computers, inexpensive and thus accessible to many who were otherwise too poor to afford them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup>
</p><p>Even with new products, such as better seeds, or greater volumes of them, such as industrial production, the poor still require access to these products. Improving road and transportation infrastructure helps solve this major bottleneck. In Africa, it costs more to move fertilizer from an African seaport 100 kilometres (60Â mi) inland than to ship it from the United States to Africa because of sparse, low-quality roads, leading to fertilizer costs two to six times the world average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Microfranchising" title="Microfranchising">Microfranchising</a> models such as door-to-door distributors who earn commission-based income or <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a>'s successful distribution system<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> are used to disseminate basic needs to remote areas for below market prices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-microfranchising_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-microfranchising-185">[185]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care_and_education">Health care and education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Health care and education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_care_system" title="Health care system">Health care system</a> and <a href="/wiki/Primary_education" title="Primary education">Primary education</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nigerian_Surgery_Table.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Nigerian_Surgery_Table.jpg/220px-Nigerian_Surgery_Table.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Nigerian_Surgery_Table.jpg/330px-Nigerian_Surgery_Table.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Nigerian_Surgery_Table.jpg/440px-Nigerian_Surgery_Table.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nigerian_Surgery_Table.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hardwood surgical tables are commonplace in rural <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigerian</a> clinics.</div></div></div>
<p>Nations do not necessarily need wealth to gain health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disease_Control_Priorities_Project_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disease_Control_Priorities_Project-186">[186]</a></sup> For example, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> had a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality_rate" title="Maternal mortality rate">maternal mortality rate</a> of 2% in the 1930s, higher than any nation today.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-post-187">[187]</a></sup> It reduced it to 0.5â0.6% in the 1950s and to 0.6% today while spending less each year on <a href="/wiki/Maternal_health" title="Maternal health">maternal health</a> because it learned what worked and what did not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post_187-1"><a href="#cite_note-post-187">[187]</a></sup> Knowledge on the cost effectiveness of healthcare interventions can be elusive and educational measures have been made to disseminate what works, such as the <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Consensus" title="Copenhagen Consensus">Copenhagen Consensus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> Cheap <a href="/wiki/Water_filter" title="Water filter">water filters</a> and promoting hand washing are some of the most cost effective health interventions and can cut <a href="/wiki/Child_mortality" title="Child mortality">deaths</a> from <a href="/wiki/Diarrhea" title="Diarrhea">diarrhea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup>
</p><p>Strategies to provide education cost effectively include <a href="/wiki/Deworming" title="Deworming">deworming</a> children, which costs about 50 cents per child per year and reduces non-attendance from <a href="/wiki/Anemia" title="Anemia">anemia</a>, illness and malnutrition, while being only a twenty-fifth as expensive as increasing school attendance by constructing schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> Schoolgirl absenteeism could be cut in half by simply providing free <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sanitary_towel" title="Sanitary towel">sanitary towels</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Food_fortification" title="Food fortification">Fortification</a> with <a href="/wiki/Micronutrient" title="Micronutrient">micronutrients</a> was ranked the most cost effective aid strategy by the Copenhagen Consensus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> For example, <a href="/wiki/Iodised_salt" title="Iodised salt">iodised salt</a> costs 2 to 3 cents per person a year while even moderate <a href="/wiki/Iodine_deficiency" title="Iodine deficiency">iodine deficiency</a> in pregnancy shaves off 10 to 15 <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_quotient" title="Intelligence quotient">IQ</a> points.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> Paying for school meals is argued to be an efficient strategy in increasing school enrollment, reducing absenteeism and increasing student attention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup>
</p><p>Desirable actions such as enrolling children in school or receiving vaccinations can be encouraged by a form of aid known as <a href="/wiki/Conditional_cash_transfer" title="Conditional cash transfer">conditional cash transfers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brazil_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brazil-196">[196]</a></sup> In Mexico, for example, dropout rates of 16- to 19-year-olds in rural area dropped by 20% and children gained half an inch in height.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-csm_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-csm-197">[197]</a></sup> Initial fears that the program would encourage families to stay at home rather than work to collect benefits have proven to be unfounded. Instead, there is less excuse for neglectful behavior as, for example, children stopped begging on the streets instead of going to school because it could result in suspension from the program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-csm_197-1"><a href="#cite_note-csm-197">[197]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Right_to_housing" title="Right to housing">right to adequete housing</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human right</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> Policies such as <a href="/wiki/Housing_First" title="Housing First">Housing First</a> emphasize that other basic needs are easier to be met when housing is first guaranteed.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Removing_constraints_on_government_services">Removing constraints on government services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Removing constraints on government services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Political_corruption" title="Political corruption">Political corruption</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tax_havens" title="Tax havens">Tax havens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transfer_mispricing" title="Transfer mispricing">Transfer mispricing</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_countries%27_debt" title="Developing countries' debt">Developing countries' debt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Conditionality" title="Conditionality">Conditionality</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Waiting_for_goods.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Waiting_for_goods.JPG/220px-Waiting_for_goods.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Waiting_for_goods.JPG/330px-Waiting_for_goods.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Waiting_for_goods.JPG/440px-Waiting_for_goods.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Waiting_for_goods.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Local citizens from the Jana bi Village wait their turn to gather goods from the <a href="/wiki/Sons_of_Iraq" title="Sons of Iraq">Sons of Iraq</a> (Abna al-Iraq) in a military operation conducted in Yusufiyah, Iraq.</div></div></div>
<p>Government revenue can be diverted away from basic services by corruption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unodc_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-unodc-200">[200]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> Funds from aid and natural resources are often sent by government individuals for <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a> to overseas banks which insist on <a href="/wiki/Bank_secrecy" title="Bank secrecy">bank secrecy</a>, instead of spending on the poor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-graft_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-graft-202">[202]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Global_Witness" title="Global Witness">Global Witness</a> report asked for more action from Western banks as they have proved capable of stanching the flow of funds linked to terrorism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-graft_202-1"><a href="#cite_note-graft-202">[202]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Illicit_financial_flows" title="Illicit financial flows">Illicit capital flight</a>, such as corporate <a href="/wiki/Tax_avoidance" title="Tax avoidance">tax avoidance</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> from the developing world is estimated at ten times the size of aid it receives and twice the debt service it pays,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> with one estimate that most of Africa would be developed if the taxes owed were paid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> About 60 per cent of illicit capital flight from Africa is from <a href="/wiki/Transfer_mispricing" title="Transfer mispricing">transfer mispricing</a>, where a <a href="/wiki/Subsidiary" title="Subsidiary">subsidiary</a> in a developing nation sells to another subsidiary or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shell_company" title="Shell company">shell company</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a> at an artificially low price to pay less tax.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-transparency_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-transparency-206">[206]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> report estimates that about 30% of sub-Saharan Africa's GDP has been moved to tax havens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-207">[207]</a></sup> Solutions include corporate "country-by-country reporting" where corporations disclose activities in each country and thereby prohibit the use of tax havens where no effective economic activity occurs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-transparency_206-1"><a href="#cite_note-transparency-206">[206]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_countries%27_debt" title="Developing countries' debt">Developing countries' debt service</a> to banks and governments from richer countries can constrain government spending on the poor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> For example, <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> spent 40% of its total budget to repay foreign debt, and only 7% for basic state services in 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldcentric.org_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-worldcentric.org-209">[209]</a></sup> One of the proposed ways to help poor countries has been <a href="/wiki/Debt_relief" title="Debt relief">debt relief</a>. Zambia began offering services, such as free health care even while overwhelming the health care infrastructure, because of savings that resulted from a 2005 round of debt relief.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> Since that round of debt relief, private creditors accounted for an increasing share of poor countries' debt service obligations. This complicated efforts to renegotiate easier terms for borrowers during crises such as the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> because the multiple private creditors involved say they have a fiduciary obligation to their clients such as the pension funds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, as primary holders of developing countries' debt, attach <a href="/wiki/Structural_adjustment" title="Structural adjustment">structural adjustment</a> <a href="/wiki/Conditionality" title="Conditionality">conditionalities</a> in return for loans which are generally geared toward loan repayment with <a href="/wiki/Austerity" title="Austerity">austerity</a> measures such as the elimination of state subsidies and the privatization of state services. For example, the World Bank presses poor nations to eliminate subsidies for fertilizer even while many farmers cannot afford them at market prices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malawi_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-Malawi-213">[213]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a>, almost 5 million of its 13 million people used to need emergency food aid but after the government changed policy and subsidies for fertilizer and seed were introduced, farmers produced record-breaking corn harvests in 2006 and 2007 as Malawi became a major food exporter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malawi_213-1"><a href="#cite_note-Malawi-213">[213]</a></sup> A major proportion of aid from donor nations is <a href="/wiki/Tied_aid" title="Tied aid">tied</a>, mandating that a receiving nation spend on products and expertise originating only from the donor country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> US law requires <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_aid" title="Food aid">food aid</a> be spent on buying food at home, instead of where the hungry live, and, as a result, half of what is spent is used on transport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Distressed_securities_fund" title="Distressed securities fund">Distressed securities funds</a>, also known as <i>vulture funds</i>, buy up the debt of poor nations cheaply and then sue countries for the full value of the debt plus interest which can be ten or 100 times what they paid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vulture_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-vulture-216">[216]</a></sup> They may pursue any companies which do business with their target country to force them to pay to the fund instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vulture_216-1"><a href="#cite_note-vulture-216">[216]</a></sup> Considerable resources are diverted on costly court cases. For example, a court in <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a> ordered the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> to pay an American speculator $100 million in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vulture_216-2"><a href="#cite_note-vulture-216">[216]</a></sup> Now, the UK, <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a> and Jersey have banned such payments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vulture_216-3"><a href="#cite_note-vulture-216">[216]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Familiy_Planning_Ethiopia_(bad_effects).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2276" data-file-width="2780" decoding="async" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Familiy_Planning_Ethiopia_%28bad_effects%29.jpg/220px-Familiy_Planning_Ethiopia_%28bad_effects%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Familiy_Planning_Ethiopia_%28bad_effects%29.jpg/330px-Familiy_Planning_Ethiopia_%28bad_effects%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Familiy_Planning_Ethiopia_%28bad_effects%29.jpg/440px-Familiy_Planning_Ethiopia_%28bad_effects%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Familiy_Planning_Ethiopia_(bad_effects).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">family planning</a> placard in <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>. It shows some negative effects of having too many children.</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Reversing_brain_drain">Reversing brain drain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Reversing brain drain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Reverse_brain_drain" title="Reverse brain drain">Reverse brain drain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_capital_flight" title="Human capital flight">Human capital flight</a></div>
<p>The loss of basic needs providers emigrating from impoverished countries has a damaging effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Philippines_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-Philippines-217">[217]</a></sup> As of 2004, there were more Ethiopia-trained doctors living in Chicago than in Ethiopia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> Proposals to mitigate the problem include compulsory government service for graduates of public medical and nursing schools<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Philippines_217-1"><a href="#cite_note-Philippines-217">[217]</a></sup> and promoting <a href="/wiki/Medical_tourism" title="Medical tourism">medical tourism</a> so that health care personnel have more incentive to practice in their home countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> It is very easy for Ugandan doctors to emigrate to other countries. It is seen that only 69% of the health care jobs were filled in Uganda. Other Ugandan doctors were seeking jobs in other countries leaving inadequate or less skilled doctors to stay in Uganda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Preventing_overpopulation">Preventing overpopulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Preventing overpopulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographic_transition" title="Demographic transition">Demographic transition</a> and <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">family planning</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Total_Fertility_Rate_Map_by_Country.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="566" data-file-width="1104" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Total_Fertility_Rate_Map_by_Country.svg/270px-Total_Fertility_Rate_Map_by_Country.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Total_Fertility_Rate_Map_by_Country.svg/405px-Total_Fertility_Rate_Map_by_Country.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Total_Fertility_Rate_Map_by_Country.svg/540px-Total_Fertility_Rate_Map_by_Country.svg.png 2x" width="270"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Total_Fertility_Rate_Map_by_Country.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of countries and territories by <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">fertility rate</a> as of 2020</div></div></div>
<p>Poverty and lack of access to birth control can lead to population increases that put pressure on local economies and access to resources, amplifying other economic inequality and creating increase poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-birthrates_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-birthrates-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> Better <a href="/wiki/Female_education" title="Female education">education for both men and women</a>, and more control of their lives, reduces population growth due to <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">family planning</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-empower_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-empower-223">[223]</a></sup> According to United Nations Population Fund (UNFPA), men and women who receive better education can earn money for their lives, strengthening economic security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Increasing_personal_income">Increasing personal income</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Increasing personal income">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following are strategies used or proposed to increase personal incomes among the poor. Raising farm incomes is described as the core of the antipoverty effort as three-quarters of the poor today are farmers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-agriculture_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-agriculture-225">[225]</a></sup> Estimates show that growth in the agricultural productivity of small farmers is, on average, at least twice as effective in benefiting the poorest half of a country's population as growth generated in nonagricultural sectors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Income_grants">Income grants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Income grants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Guaranteed_minimum_income" title="Guaranteed minimum income">Guaranteed minimum income</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_security" title="Social security">Social security</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Welfare" title="Welfare">Welfare</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Afghan_girl_begging.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="867" data-file-width="1300" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Afghan_girl_begging.jpg/220px-Afghan_girl_begging.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Afghan_girl_begging.jpg/330px-Afghan_girl_begging.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Afghan_girl_begging.jpg/440px-Afghan_girl_begging.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Afghan_girl_begging.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Afghan girl begging in <a href="/wiki/Kabul" title="Kabul">Kabul</a></div></div></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Guaranteed_minimum_income" title="Guaranteed minimum income">guaranteed minimum income</a> ensures that every citizen will be able to purchase a desired level of basic needs. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basic_income" title="Basic income">basic income</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Negative_income_tax" title="Negative income tax">negative income tax</a>) is a system of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_security" title="Social security">social security</a>, that periodically provides each citizen, rich or poor, with a sum of money that is sufficient to live on. Studies of large cash-transfer programs in Ethiopia, Kenya, and Malawi show that the programs can be effective in increasing consumption, schooling, and nutrition, whether they are tied to such conditions or not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spiegel_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-Spiegel-228">[228]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Namibians_line_up_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-Namibians_line_up-229">[229]</a></sup> Proponents argue that a basic income is more economically efficient than a <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unemployment_benefit" title="Unemployment benefit">unemployment benefits</a>, as the minimum wage effectively imposes a high marginal tax on employers, causing <a href="/wiki/Deadweight_loss" title="Deadweight loss">losses in efficiency</a>. In 1968, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Samuelson" title="Paul Samuelson">Paul Samuelson</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Kenneth_Galbraith" title="John Kenneth Galbraith">John Kenneth Galbraith</a> and another 1,200 economists signed a document calling for the US Congress to introduce a system of income guarantees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> Winners of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Economics" title="Nobel Prize in Economics">Nobel Prize in Economics</a>, with often diverse political convictions, who support a basic income include <a href="/wiki/Herbert_A._Simon" title="Herbert A. Simon">Herbert A. Simon</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Standing_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-Standing-231">[231]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Hayek" title="Friedrich Hayek">Friedrich Hayek</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Solow" title="Robert Solow">Robert Solow</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Standing_231-1"><a href="#cite_note-Standing-231">[231]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Milton_Friedman" title="Milton Friedman">Milton Friedman</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jan_Tinbergen" title="Jan Tinbergen">Jan Tinbergen</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Standing_231-2"><a href="#cite_note-Standing-231">[231]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Tobin" title="James Tobin">James Tobin</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steensland_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-Steensland-234">[234]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup>
and <a href="/wiki/James_Meade" title="James Meade">James Meade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Standing_231-3"><a href="#cite_note-Standing-231">[231]</a></sup>
</p><p>Income grants are argued to be vastly more efficient in extending basic needs to the poor than <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subsidies" title="Subsidies">subsidizing</a> supplies whose effectiveness in poverty alleviation is diluted by the non-poor who enjoy the same subsidized prices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> With cars and other appliances, the wealthiest 20% of Egypt uses about 93% of the country's fuel subsidies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fossilfuel_238-0"><a href="#cite_note-fossilfuel-238">[238]</a></sup> In some countries, fuel subsidies are a larger part of the budget than health and education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fossilfuel_238-1"><a href="#cite_note-fossilfuel-238">[238]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> A 2008 study concluded that the money spent on in-kind transfers in India in a year could lift all India's poor out of poverty for that year if transferred directly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> The primary obstacle argued against direct cash transfers is the impractically for poor countries of such large and direct transfers. In practice, payments determined by complex iris scanning are used by war-torn <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of Congo">Democratic Republic of Congo</a> and Afghanistan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> while India is phasing out its fuel subsidies in favor of direct transfers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> Additionally, in aid models, the <a href="/wiki/Famine_relief" title="Famine relief">famine relief</a> model increasingly used by aid groups calls for giving cash or cash vouchers to the hungry to pay local farmers instead of buying food from donor countries, often required by law, as it wastes money on transport costs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-csmonitor_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-csmonitor-243">[243]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wfp_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-wfp-244">[244]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_freedoms">Economic freedoms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Economic freedoms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Economic_freedom" title="Economic freedom">Economic freedom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Red_tape" title="Red tape">Red tape</a></div>
<p>Corruption often leads to many <a href="/wiki/Civil_service" title="Civil service">civil services</a> being treated by governments as employment agencies to loyal supporters<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup> and so it could mean going through 20 procedures, paying $2,696 in fees, and waiting 82 business days to start a business in <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>, while in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> it takes two days, two registration procedures, and $280 to do the same.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> Such costly barriers favor big firms at the expense of small enterprises, where most jobs are created.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cato_247-0"><a href="#cite_note-cato-247">[247]</a></sup> Often, businesses have to bribe government officials even for routine activities, which is, in effect, a tax on business.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-macroeconomics1_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-macroeconomics1-248">[248]</a></sup> Noted reductions in poverty in recent decades has occurred in China and India mostly as a result of the abandonment of <a href="/wiki/Collective_farming" title="Collective farming">collective farming</a> in China and the ending of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_planning" title="Central planning">central planning</a> model known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/License_Raj" title="License Raj">License Raj</a> in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc1_249-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1-249">[249]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> concludes that governments and feudal elites extending to the poor the right to the land that they live and use are 'the key to reducing poverty' citing that land rights greatly increase poor people's wealth, in some cases doubling it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-landrights_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-landrights-252">[252]</a></sup> Although approaches varied, the World Bank said the key issues were security of tenure and ensuring land transactions costs were low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-landrights_252-1"><a href="#cite_note-landrights-252">[252]</a></sup>
</p><p>Greater access to markets brings more income to the poor. Road infrastructure has a direct impact on poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCR_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-GCR-253">[253]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup> Additionally, migration from poorer countries resulted in $328 billion sent from richer to poorer countries in 2010, more than double the $120 billion in official aid flows from <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> members. In 2011, India got $52 billion from its <a href="/wiki/Diaspora" title="Diaspora">diaspora</a>, more than it took in <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_services">Financial services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Financial services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Microfinance" title="Microfinance">Microfinance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microcredit" title="Microcredit">Microcredit</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kiwanja_uganda_charging_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="876" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Kiwanja_uganda_charging_1.jpg/220px-Kiwanja_uganda_charging_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Kiwanja_uganda_charging_1.jpg/330px-Kiwanja_uganda_charging_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Kiwanja_uganda_charging_1.jpg/440px-Kiwanja_uganda_charging_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kiwanja_uganda_charging_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Information and communication technologies for development help to fight poverty.</div></div></div>
<p>Microloans, made famous by the <a href="/wiki/Grameen_Bank" title="Grameen Bank">Grameen Bank</a>, is where small amounts of money are loaned to farmers or villages, mostly women, who can then obtain physical capital to increase their economic rewards. However, microlending has been criticized for making hyperprofits off the poor even from its founder, <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Yunus" title="Muhammad Yunus">Muhammad Yunus</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup> and in India, <a href="/wiki/Arundhati_Roy" title="Arundhati Roy">Arundhati Roy</a> asserts that some 250,000 debt-ridden farmers have been driven to suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup>
</p><p>Those in poverty place overwhelming importance on having a safe place to save money, much more so than receiving loans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time.com_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-time.com-260">[260]</a></sup> Additionally, a large part of <a href="/wiki/Microfinance" title="Microfinance">microfinance</a> loans are spent not on investments but on products that would usually be paid by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Checking_account" title="Checking account">checking</a> or <a href="/wiki/Savings_account" title="Savings account">savings account</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time.com_260-1"><a href="#cite_note-time.com-260">[260]</a></sup> Microsavings are designs to make savings products available for the poor, who make small deposits. <a href="/wiki/Mobile_banking" title="Mobile banking">Mobile banking</a> utilizes the wide availability of mobile phones to address the problem of the heavy regulation and costly maintenance of saving accounts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time.com_260-2"><a href="#cite_note-time.com-260">[260]</a></sup> This usually involves a network of agents of mostly shopkeepers, instead of bank branches, would take deposits in cash and translate these onto a virtual account on customers' phones. Cash transfers can be done between phones and issued back in cash with a small commission, making <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittances</a> safer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-safaricom_261-0"><a href="#cite_note-safaricom-261">[261]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reversing_wealth_concentration">Reversing wealth concentration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Reversing wealth concentration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a>, among others, has called for an international movement to end extreme wealth concentration arguing that the concentration of resources in the hands of the top 1% depresses economic activity and makes life harder for everyone elseâparticularly those at the bottom of the economic ladder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP-20130120_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-WP-20130120-262">[262]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-20130118_263-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-20130118-263">[263]</a></sup> And they say that the gains of the world's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Billionaires" title="Billionaires">billionaires</a> in 2017, which amounted to $762 billion, were enough to end extreme global poverty seven times over.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Perspectives">Perspectives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Perspectives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_theories">Economic theories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Economic theories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Causes_of_poverty" title="Causes of poverty">Causes of poverty</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20220801_Economic_stratification_-_cross-class_friendships_-_bar_chart.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="675" data-file-width="1250" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/20220801_Economic_stratification_-_cross-class_friendships_-_bar_chart.svg/330px-20220801_Economic_stratification_-_cross-class_friendships_-_bar_chart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/20220801_Economic_stratification_-_cross-class_friendships_-_bar_chart.svg/495px-20220801_Economic_stratification_-_cross-class_friendships_-_bar_chart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/20220801_Economic_stratification_-_cross-class_friendships_-_bar_chart.svg/660px-20220801_Economic_stratification_-_cross-class_friendships_-_bar_chart.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20220801_Economic_stratification_-_cross-class_friendships_-_bar_chart.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Data shows substantial social segregation correlating with economic income groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EconomicStratification_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-EconomicStratification-265">[265]</a></sup> However, social connectedness to people of higher income levels is a strong predictor of upward income mobility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EconomicStratification_265-1"><a href="#cite_note-EconomicStratification-265">[265]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The cause of poverty is a highly ideologically charged subject, as different causes point to different remedies. Very broadly speaking, the <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialist</a> tradition locates the roots of poverty in problems of distribution and the use of the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a> as capital benefiting individuals, and calls for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Redistribution_of_wealth" title="Redistribution of wealth">redistribution of wealth</a> as the solution, whereas the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neoliberal" title="Neoliberal">neoliberal</a> school of thought holds that creating conditions for profitable private investment is the solution. Neoliberal <a href="/wiki/Think_tank" title="Think tank">think tanks</a> have received extensive funding,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup> and the ability to apply many of their ideas in highly indebted countries in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_South" title="Global South">global South</a> as a condition for receiving emergency loans from the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>.
</p><p>The existence of inequality is in part due to a set of self-reinforcing behaviors that all together constitute one aspect of the <a href="/wiki/Cycle_of_poverty" title="Cycle of poverty">cycle of poverty</a>. These behaviors, in addition to unfavorable, external circumstances, also explain the existence of the <a href="/wiki/Matthew_effect" title="Matthew effect">Matthew effect</a>, which not only exacerbates existing inequality, but is more likely to make it multigenerational. Widespread, multigenerational poverty is an important contributor to civil unrest and political instability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> For example, <a href="/wiki/Raghuram_Rajan" title="Raghuram Rajan">Raghuram G. Rajan</a>, former governor of the <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Bank_of_India" title="Reserve Bank of India">Reserve Bank of India</a> and former chief economist at the International Monetary Fund, has blamed the ever-widening gulf between the rich and the poor, especially <a href="/wiki/Income_inequality_in_the_United_States" title="Income inequality in the United States">in the US</a>, to be one of the main fault lines which caused the financial institutions to pump money into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subprime_mortgages" title="Subprime mortgages">subprime mortgages</a>âon political behest, as a palliative and not a remedy, for povertyâcausing the <a href="/wiki/Subprime_mortgage_crisis" title="Subprime mortgage crisis">financial crisis of 2007â2009</a>. In Rajan's view the main cause of the increasing gap between high income and low income earners was lack of equal access to higher education for the latter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Empirical_evidence" title="Empirical evidence">data based</a> scientific <a href="/wiki/Empirical_research" title="Empirical research">empirical research</a>, which studied the impact of <a href="/wiki/Political_family" title="Political family">dynastic politics</a> on the level of poverty of the provinces, found a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Correlation_and_dependence" title="Correlation and dependence">positive correlation</a> between dynastic politics and poverty; i.e. the higher proportion of dynastic politicians in power in a province leads to higher poverty rate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup> There is significant evidence that these political dynasties use their political dominance over their respective regions to enrich themselves, using methods such as graft or outright bribery of legislators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enough8_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-enough8-270">[270]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmentalism">Environmentalism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Environmentalism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism_of_the_poor" title="Environmentalism of the poor">Environmentalism of the poor</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_and_poverty" title="Climate change and poverty">Climate change and poverty</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Depuradora_de_Lluc.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Depuradora_de_Lluc.JPG/250px-Depuradora_de_Lluc.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Depuradora_de_Lluc.JPG/375px-Depuradora_de_Lluc.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Depuradora_de_Lluc.JPG/500px-Depuradora_de_Lluc.JPG 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Depuradora_de_Lluc.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Sewage_treatment" title="Sewage treatment">sewage treatment</a> plant that uses <a href="/wiki/Solar_energy" title="Solar energy">solar energy</a>, located at <a href="/wiki/Santuari_de_Lluc" title="Santuari de Lluc">Santuari de Lluc</a> monastery, Majorca</div></div></div>
<p>Important studies such as the <a href="/wiki/Our_Common_Future" title="Our Common Future">Brundtland Report</a> concluded that poverty causes environmental degradation, while other theories like <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism_of_the_poor" title="Environmentalism of the poor">environmentalism of the poor</a> conclude that the global poor may be the most important force for sustainability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup> Either way, the poor suffer most from environmental degradation caused by reckless <a href="/wiki/Exploitation_of_natural_resources" title="Exploitation of natural resources">exploitation of natural resources</a> by the rich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> This unfair distribution of environmental burdens and benefits has generated the global <a href="/wiki/Environmental_justice" title="Environmental justice">environmental justice</a> movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup>
</p><p>A report published in 2013 by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, with support from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_%26_Development_Knowledge_Network" title="Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network">Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network</a>, found that climate change was likely to hinder future attempts to reduce poverty. The report presented the likely impacts of present day, 2Â Â°C and 4Â Â°C warming on agricultural production, water resources, coastal ecosystems and cities across Sub-Saharan Africa, South Asia and South East Asia. The impacts of a temperature rise of 2Â Â°C included: regular food shortages in Sub-Saharan Africa; shifting rain patterns in South Asia leaving some parts under water and others without enough water for power generation, irrigation or drinking; degradation and loss of reefs in South East Asia, resulting in reduced fish stocks; and coastal communities and cities more vulnerable to increasingly violent storms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup> In 2016, a UN report claimed that by 2030, an additional 122 million more people could be driven to extreme poverty because of climate change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup>
</p><p>Global warming can also lead to a deficiency in water availability; with higher temperatures and CO<sub>2</sub> levels, plants consume more water leaving less for people. By consequence, water in rivers and streams will decline in the mid-altitude regions like Central Asia, Europe and North America. And if CO<sub>2</sub> levels continue to rise, or even remain the same, droughts will be happening much faster and will be lasting longer. According to a 2016 study led by Professor of Water Management, Arjen Hoekstra, four billion people are affected by water scarcity at least one month per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spirituality">Spirituality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Poverty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Spirituality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Simple_living" title="Simple living">Simple living</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_counsels" title="Evangelical counsels">Evangelical counsels</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Giotto_-_Legend_of_St_Francis_-_-05-_-_Renunciation_of_Wordly_Goods.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="746" data-file-width="652" decoding="async" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Giotto_-_Legend_of_St_Francis_-_-05-_-_Renunciation_of_Wordly_Goods.jpg/220px-Giotto_-_Legend_of_St_Francis_-_-05-_-_Renunciation_of_Wordly_Goods.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Giotto_-_Legend_of_St_Francis_-_-05-_-_Renunciation_of_Wordly_Goods.jpg/330px-Giotto_-_Legend_of_St_Francis_-_-05-_-_Renunciation_of_Wordly_Goods.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Giotto_-_Legend_of_St_Francis_-_-05-_-_Renunciation_of_Wordly_Goods.jpg/440px-Giotto_-_Legend_of_St_Francis_-_-05-_-_Renunciation_of_Wordly_Goods.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Giotto_-_Legend_of_St_Francis_-_-05-_-_Renunciation_of_Wordly_Goods.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>St. <a href="/wiki/Francis_of_Assisi" title="Francis of Assisi">Francis of Assisi</a> renounces his worldly goods in a painting attributed to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Giotto_di_Bondone" title="Giotto di Bondone">Giotto di Bondone</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Among some individuals, poverty is considered a necessary or desirable condition, which must be embraced to reach certain spiritual, moral, or intellectual states. Poverty is often understood to be an essential element of <a href="/wiki/Nekkhamma" title="Nekkhamma">renunciation</a> in religions such as <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> (only for monks, not for lay persons) and <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a>, whilst in <a href="/wiki/Christian_views_on_poverty_and_wealth" title="Christian views on poverty and wealth">Christianity</a>, in particular Roman Catholicism, it is one of the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_counsels" title="Evangelical counsels">evangelical counsels</a>.  The main aim of giving up things of the materialistic world is to withdraw oneself from sensual pleasures (as they are considered illusionary and only temporary in some religionsâsuch as the concept of <a href="/wiki/Dunya" title="Dunya">dunya</a> in <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>). This self-invited poverty (or giving up pleasures) is different from the one caused by economic imbalance.
</p><p>Some Christian communities, such as the <a href="/wiki/The_Simple_Way" title="The Simple Way">Simple Way</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bruderhof_Communities" title="Bruderhof Communities">Bruderhof</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Amish" title="Amish">Amish</a> value voluntary poverty;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> some even take a vow of poverty, similar to that of the traditional Catholic orders, in order to live a more complete life of discipleship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oved_2017_278-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oved_2017-278">[278]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benedict_XVI" title="Benedict XVI">Benedict XVI</a> distinguished "poverty <i>chosen</i>" (the poverty of spirit proposed by Jesus), and "poverty <i>to be fought</i>" (unjust and imposed poverty). He considered that the moderation implied in the former favors solidarity, and is a necessary condition so as to fight effectively to eradicate the abuse of the latter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup>
</p><p>As it was indicated above the reduction of poverty results from <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religion</a>, but also can result from <a href="/wiki/Solidarity" title="Solidarity">solidarity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup>
</p>
